              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15632828522685072474">"The Eighth Sister" is the first book in Dugoni's Charles Jenkins espionage series, currently a series of two books. Like the famous Russian nesting dolls, Dugoni has provided us not just with an espionage story, but another story hidden within that espionage story or perhaps framing it. The espionage story is top notch (particularly if you buy the setup) and takes us into the heart Putin's Russia, a world of suspicions, and spy games set in play decades earlier when there were two Cold War powe</span>
  <span id="freeText15632828522685072474" style="display:none">"The Eighth Sister" is the first book in Dugoni's Charles Jenkins espionage series, currently a series of two books. Like the famous Russian nesting dolls, Dugoni has provided us not just with an espionage story, but another story hidden within that espionage story or perhaps framing it. The espionage story is top notch (particularly if you buy the setup) and takes us into the heart Putin's Russia, a world of suspicions, and spy games set in play decades earlier when there were two Cold War powers facing off Mano to Mano. Dugoni is especially adept as showing us how the spy game is like a chessboard with two opponents squaring off, trying to out-think the other twenty moves ahead. Make no mistake this is an action-packed, hold-your-breath adventure. But then, there's more at foot than just spygames, and we get a courtroom drama with betrayals, treachery, and levels of subterfuge. Overall, just a terrific read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15632828522685072474" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2701024725" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2701024725" />
    <a title="Sandy *The world could end while I was reading and I would never notice*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30817744-sandy-the-world-could-end-while-i-was-reading-and-i-would-never-notice"><img alt="Sandy *The world could end while I was reading and I would never notice*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509647506p2/30817744.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2701024725?book_show_action=true">Nov 18, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sandy *The world could end while I was reading and I would never notice*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sandy *The world could end while I was reading and I would never notice*" href="/user/show/30817744-sandy-the-world-could-end-while-i-was-reading-and-i-would-never-notice">Sandy *The world could end while I was reading and I would never notice*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30817744-sandy-the-world-could-end-while-i-was-reading-and-i-would-never-notice?shelf=3-star">3-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30817744-sandy-the-world-could-end-while-i-was-reading-and-i-would-never-notice?shelf=4-star">4-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30817744-sandy-the-world-could-end-while-i-was-reading-and-i-would-never-notice?shelf=contemporary-fiction">contemporary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30817744-sandy-the-world-could-end-while-i-was-reading-and-i-would-never-notice?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30817744-sandy-the-world-could-end-while-i-was-reading-and-i-would-never-notice?shelf=netgalley-arc">netgalley-arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30817744-sandy-the-world-could-end-while-i-was-reading-and-i-would-never-notice?shelf=spy-thriller">spy-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30817744-sandy-the-world-could-end-while-i-was-reading-and-i-would-never-notice?shelf=legal-thriller">legal-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30817744-sandy-the-world-could-end-while-i-was-reading-and-i-would-never-notice?shelf=series">series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2701024725" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3923272459344144673">EXCERPT: The bus wound its way along the Moskva River, already filling with chunks of floating ice, another harbinger of the wicked winter to come. Thirty minutes after Zarina boarded, the bus reached her stop in front of the supermarket on Filevsky Bulvar. She crossed the bleak park, listening to the spindling tree limbs click and clack with each wind gust. Soviet-era apartment buildings stood like sentries around the park, grotesque concrete blocks with tiny windows and tagged with graffiti. Z</span>
  <span id="freeText3923272459344144673" style="display:none">EXCERPT: The bus wound its way along the Moskva River, already filling with chunks of floating ice, another harbinger of the wicked winter to come. Thirty minutes after Zarina boarded, the bus reached her stop in front of the supermarket on Filevsky Bulvar. She crossed the bleak park, listening to the spindling tree limbs click and clack with each wind gust. Soviet-era apartment buildings stood like sentries around the park, grotesque concrete blocks with tiny windows and tagged with graffiti. Zarina pushed open a brown metal door to a spartan lobby.The light fixtures had long ago been stolen - along with the marble floor and brass stair railing. Russians had interpreted capitalism to mean: "Steal what you can sell." Attempts to replenish the buildings had only led to more thefts. <br /><br />Zarina rode the elevator to the twelfth floor and stepped into a hallway as drab and bare as the lobby. She undid the four locks to what had once been her parents' apartment, wiped the soles of her boots on the mat so as not to mark the oak floor, inlaid with an intricate geometric design, and hung her coat and hat on the rack before she stepped into the living area. <br /><br />"We were beginning to wonder if you were coming home, Ms Kazakova." <br /><br />The man's voice startled her, and Zarina screamed.<br /><br />ABOUT THIS BOOK: Former CIA case officer Charles Jenkins is a man at a crossroads: in his early sixties, he has a family, a new baby on the way, and a security consulting business on the brink of bankruptcy. Then his former bureau chief shows up at his house with a risky new assignment: travel undercover to Moscow and locate a Russian agent believed to be killing members of a clandestine US spy cell known as the seven sisters.<br /><br />Desperate for money, Jenkins agrees to the mission and heads to the Russian capital. But when he finds the mastermind agent behind the assassinations—the so-called eighth sister—she is not who or what he was led to believe. Then again, neither is anyone else in this deadly game of cat and mouse.<br /><br />Pursued by a dogged Russian intelligence officer, Jenkins executes a daring escape across the Black Sea, only to find himself abandoned by the agency he serves. With his family and freedom at risk, Jenkins is in the fight of his life—against his own country.<br /><br />MY THOUGHTS: I am not a fan of the spy-thriller/legal thriller genres, and had this book been written by anyone other than Robert Dugoni, I may not have finished it. Even so, I struggled at times to maintain my interest. And, if I have to be honest, I probably didn't check out the subject matter as carefully as I should have before hitting the 'request' button. Just seeing the Robert Dugoni name was recommendation enough for me.<br /><br />And as I said, if The Eighth Sister had been written by anyone other than Dugoni, I probably wouldn't have finished it. However, his writing style carried me through; that and the mystery of the eight 'sisters', a spy ring.<br /><br />While this is definitely not my favorite of Dugoni's books, it is certainly to be recommended if you are a spy-thriller aficionado.I am glad I read it, but not entirely sure that I want to repeat the experience with more of this series to come. <br /><br />#The Eighth Sister #NetGalley<br /><br />***.5<br /><br />THE AUTHOR: Robert Dugoni is the New York Times, #1 Amazon, and #1 Wall Street Journal Bestselling Author of the Tracy Crosswhite series. He is also the author of the critically acclaimed The Extraordinary Life of Sam Hell, released April 2018. Dugoni's first series featured attorney David Sloane and CIA agent Charles Jenkins, both of whom appear in The Eighth Sister.<br /><br />DISCLOSURE: Thank you to Thomas &amp; Mercer via Netgalley for providing a digital ARC of The Eighth Sister by Robert Dugoni for review. All opinions expressed in this review are entirely my own opinions.<br /><br />For an explanation of my rating system, please refer to my Goodreads.com profile page, or the about page on sandysbookaday.wordpress.com<br /><br />This review and others are also published on Twitter, Amazon and my webpage <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://sandysbookaday.wordpress.com/2019/11/19/the-eighth-sister-by-robert-dugoni/">https://sandysbookaday.wordpress.com/...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="3923272459344144673" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2600433304?book_show_action=true">Jan 03, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrew Tucker" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrew Tucker" href="/user/show/36848955-andrew-tucker">Andrew Tucker</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2600433304" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15993282251232077007">2.5 stars rounded up to 3.<br/><br/>I have really enjoyed Dugoni's Tracy Crosswhite series so when I saw a new book from him I jumped on the chance to get an ARC from netgalley. <br/><br/>The blurb describes this book as a spy novel, but its really 60% spy novel and 40% courtroom drama. This complete change was a bit of a turnoff for me and I would have enjoyed the book a lot more if it had stayed in the spy genre and explored those topics instead of turning into legal proceedings. The main lawyer, David Sloane, is</span>
  <span id="freeText15993282251232077007" style="display:none">2.5 stars rounded up to 3.<br /><br />I have really enjoyed Dugoni's Tracy Crosswhite series so when I saw a new book from him I jumped on the chance to get an ARC from netgalley. <br /><br />The blurb describes this book as a spy novel, but its really 60% spy novel and 40% courtroom drama. This complete change was a bit of a turnoff for me and I would have enjoyed the book a lot more if it had stayed in the spy genre and explored those topics instead of turning into legal proceedings. The main lawyer, David Sloane, is the main character in another series by Dugoni and it feels more like this should have been another book in that series instead of being billed as a standalone spy novel.<br /><br />The plot was interesting though its a bit of stretch that after only 2 years in the CIA in the 1970s the protagonist would still be so valuable and skilled at spying 40 years later. My biggest beef with the spy part is soooooo many threads left unresolved. The title is Eighth Sister yet we never find out anything about her because once stuff blows up we end up in a courtroom. The motivations and reasons for the antagonist causing the main conflicts in the book are left completely unexplained. These kind floating questions left me pretty unsatisfied and is my main reason for a low rating. <br /><br />Perhaps the intent is that this the first of a series and more will be explained in a future book, but thats not what I thought I was getting and I am not sure I care enough to read a follow up to find out more of the why behind the story.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15993282251232077007" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3201401945" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3201401945" />
    <a title="The Cats’ Mother" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5720552-the-cats-mother"><img alt="The Cats’ Mother" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567802395p2/5720552.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3201401945?book_show_action=true">Sep 06, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="The Cats’ Mother" class="user" itemprop="url" name="The Cats’ Mother" href="/user/show/5720552-the-cats-mother">The Cats’ Mother</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5720552-the-cats-mother?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5720552-the-cats-mother?shelf=read-in-2020">read-in-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5720552-the-cats-mother?shelf=legal-political-or-spy-thrillers">legal-political-or-spy-thrillers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5720552-the-cats-mother?shelf=bought-e-or-a-books-read">bought-e-or-a-books-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5720552-the-cats-mother?shelf=2020-ebooks">2020-ebooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3201401945" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13240471847711738351">The Eighth Sister is a contemporary spy novel about retired CIA agent Charlie Jenkins, which features David Sloane, the hero of his other series, which I haven’t read - so I don’t know if Jenkins has appeared previously in those as a minor character or not. I bought this because I have an ARC of the sequel - The Last Agent - which is due to be published on September 22nd. I’ve read and adored all of the author’s Tracy Crosswhite series, so was looking forward to this, but unfortunately I couldn’</span>
  <span id="freeText13240471847711738351" style="display:none">The Eighth Sister is a contemporary spy novel about retired CIA agent Charlie Jenkins, which features David Sloane, the hero of his other series, which I haven’t read - so I don’t know if Jenkins has appeared previously in those as a minor character or not. I bought this because I have an ARC of the sequel - The Last Agent - which is due to be published on September 22nd. I’ve read and adored all of the author’s Tracy Crosswhite series, so was looking forward to this, but unfortunately I couldn’t engage with the main character and found it a bit of a slog.<br /><br />Charlie Jenkins, a 64 year old former spy, enjoys a quiet life with his much younger wife, nine year old son, and a baby on the way, but his private security business is in financial trouble due to an unreliable client. When his former chief of station contacts him out of the blue about a secret mission to Russia to flush out the identity of the person leaking the names of long-standing double-agents known as the Seven Sisters to the FSB, Charlie knows it’s risky, but the money on offer could save his home and livelihood as well as the lives of the remaining sisters. As a 6 foot 5 African-American, he knows he will stand out in Moscow - but that’s just the first of his difficulties as he soon learns he’s been betrayed, and nothing is as it seems...<br /><br />I do like the occasional spy thriller, although I sometimes get lost with all the machinations and double-crosses involved - and the premise of this one seemed rather far-fetched from the start. I kept wondering when the actual Eighth Sister would appear. Jenkins is portrayed as steadfast and loyal, devoted to his family and his country, but he comes across as dour and humourless which made him hard to care about. I was hoping for more excitement but even the chase scenes were rather slow and drawn out, the action only really getting going in the second half, then the final part switches to a courtroom battle, the outcome of which was never really in doubt - I was hoping for more of a twist - and ended up slightly confused by the epilogue. I did like David Sloane and his son Jake however so will be adding those books to my TBR. Dugoni is a great writer, he just didn’t hook me with this main character - hopefully he’ll grow on me for round two.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13240471847711738351" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2697499710" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer8093905381164575722">Took a different turn from CIA action to court room drama. I thought it was a bit slow but did enjoy the parts in Russia. I am not a fan of court room fiction so it did not appeal to me. Like the ending with the final phone call. Recommend to others but not my favorite of his.</span>

<div id="review_2956236462" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2956236462" />
    <a title="Alex Cantone" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48050946-alex-cantone"><img alt="Alex Cantone" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1479001219p2/48050946.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2956236462?book_show_action=true">Aug 17, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alex Cantone" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alex Cantone" href="/user/show/48050946-alex-cantone">Alex Cantone</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781503903319" href="/book/show/40383798-the-eighth-sister">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48050946-alex-cantone?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48050946-alex-cantone?shelf=2020-read">2020-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48050946-alex-cantone?shelf=russian-themed">russian-themed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48050946-alex-cantone?shelf=espionage">espionage</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2956236462" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13277747555626746433">Former CIA operative Charles Jenkins, aged 64 runs a company providing security services to investment branches located overseas, but is in financial trouble as monies owed to him by a key client to pay contractors appears to have dried up. He has mortgaged his farm on Camano Island in Puget Sound off Seattle, but with his young wife heavily pregnant with their second child, he is facing bankruptcy. Then his former station chief in Mexico City arrives on his doorstep, after forty years, offering</span>
  <span id="freeText13277747555626746433" style="display:none">Former CIA operative Charles Jenkins, aged 64 runs a company providing security services to investment branches located overseas, but is in financial trouble as monies owed to him by a key client to pay contractors appears to have dried up. He has mortgaged his farm on Camano Island in Puget Sound off Seattle, but with his young wife heavily pregnant with their second child, he is facing bankruptcy. Then his former station chief in Mexico City arrives on his doorstep, after forty years, offering him a lifeline: to go to Moscow, posing as a disgruntled former CIA agent with information to sell to the FSB, on female agents deep within the system, known as the Seven Sisters.<br /><br />This is a book in two parts: the first is a spy thriller, with Jenkins disowned as his life is in jeopardy, escaping Moscow with the help of an enigmatic young woman, chased by the FSB to Vishnevka on the east coast of the Black Sea near to Sochi, north of the border with Georgia, then by fishing boat to Istanbul and various forms of transport across Turkey to Çeşme on the Aegean, not far from the Greek Island of Chios, keeping one step ahead of the FSB. He is assisted by his friend, Seattle hot-shot lawyer, David Sloane (a character in some of the author’s other books) and his young offsider Jake, in obtaining documentation to smuggle him back to the States.<br /><br />The second part is a court-room drama, of a government cover-up, with Jenkins accused of fabricating a story to cover his actions in betraying his country to overseas interests. Sloane defends his friend, weaving his magic against a battery of government lawyers, who suppress files in the national interest. At least the judge is even-handed.<br /><br />This was the first book I had read by this author, and unfortunately it disappointed. The Black Sea area I find fascinating, both politically and its bathymetry - its depths preserving ancient wrecks in an almost pristine state. I enjoyed the tradecraft of espionage and the by-play between Federov of the FSB and Jenkins, and I added to my knowledge of Russian. The latter part might hold the interest of readers who enjoy legal thrillers, but did nothing for me. Given a choice between the dentist’s chair and sitting on a jury panel I would take the dentist’s chair every time.<br /><br />Most annoying, the fate of four of the “sisters” in the title was never resolved, and for that I will “pass” on the author’s other works.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13277747555626746433" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('YE6OkP7E19S46kHMVcoJZuRmR48+ZGKGL0P+jzwcrQxaaOdCRZoevB/B9a2iPwO5MjmgR/Dp7OF0Pbg+8V9flg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('qGEc9wCpDjQvfFtOgXndqERqv56zawk4xByEgErqvjqSR3Ulu/fHXIhX7y92jNd3kjVYVn3mh1+fYsIxh6lMoA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4528808319091493543">Robert Dugoni is the New York Times, #1 Amazon, and #1 Wall Street Journal Bestselling Author of the Tracy Crosswhite series: My Sister's Grave, Her Last Breath, In the Clearing, The Trapped Girl and Close to Home, A Steep Price and A Cold Trail as well as the short prequels The Academy and Third Watch. The police procedural featuring Seattle Homicide Detective Tracy Crosswhite has kept Dugoni in </span>
  <span id="freeText4528808319091493543" style="display:none">Robert Dugoni is the New York Times, #1 Amazon, and #1 Wall Street Journal Bestselling Author of the Tracy Crosswhite series: My Sister's Grave, Her Last Breath, In the Clearing, The Trapped Girl and Close to Home, A Steep Price and A Cold Trail as well as the short prequels The Academy and Third Watch. The police procedural featuring Seattle Homicide Detective Tracy Crosswhite has kept Dugoni in the Amazon top 10 for more than three years and sold more than 5 million copies. He is also the author of the critically acclaimed The Extraordinary Life of Sam Hell, released April 2018 and soon to be a major motion picture. He is also the author of the Charles Jenkin's International spy series, The Eighth Sister and The Last Agent, soon to be a television series. Dugoni's first series featured attorney David Sloane and CIA agent Charles Jenkins. <br />He is the winner of the Nancy Pearl Award for fiction, a two-time nominee for the Harper Lee Award for Legal Fiction, A two-time nominee for the Mystery Writer's of America Edgar Award and a two-time nominee for the International Thriller of the year. His non-fiction expose, The Cyanide Canary, was a 2004 Best Book of the Year. He is published in more than 30 countries and two dozen languages.<br />You can sign up for his newsletter at:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.robertdugoni.com">http://www.robertdugoni.com</a> and message him on facebook, twitter and instagram </span>
  <a data-text-id="4528808319091493543" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
